\section*{Appendix: Explicit Gram/Fock Construction, T-Uniformity, and Tails}\label{sec:appendix}
For $s=\sigma+it$ with $\sigma>1/2$, define block signals $\Psi_j^{(s)}(x):=\sum_{p\in B_j} p^{-\sigma}e^{-x\log p}$ and $V_s e_j:= e^{-(s-1/2)x}\Psi_j^{(s)}(x)$. Set $T(s):=V_s^{\,*}V_s$ (PSD, analytic in $s$). Then
\[
T_{mn}(\sigma)\ =\ \sum_{p\in B_m}\sum_{q\in B_n}\frac{p^{-\sigma}q^{-\sigma}}{\,2\sigma-1+\log p+\log q\,},\quad \|T(\sigma)\|_2^2\ \ll\ \Big(\sum_p \tfrac{p^{-2\sigma}}{1+2\log p}\Big)^2.
\]
Using the explicit majorant lemma and partial summation yields the far-tail bounds required for the covering budgets. Throughout, all constants are T-uniform on Whitney scale ($L=c/\log\langle T\rangle$): the Carleson box constant $C_{\rm box}^{(\mathrm{Whitney})}$ is locked, the zero-counting constants in Lemma~\ref{lem:zc} are absolute ($A_0=2$, $A_1=1/(2\pi)$), and the prime budget satisfies $C_P(\kappa(T))\le \CPstar$.
\subsection*{Proof (one–sided corridor)}
We prove \(w(t)\ge -\tfrac{\pi}{2}\) a.e.; the upper bound follows by applying the same argument to \(-w\) under \eqref{eq:phase-velocity-plus}.
\medskip
\noindent\emph{Step 1: Distributional domination implies a uniform local test inequality.}
From \eqref{eq:phase-velocity} and \eqref{eq:carleson-budget}, for every interval \(I\) and every nonnegative \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(I)\),
\begin{equation}\label{eq:test-ineq}
\int_{\mathbb R} \phi(t)\,(-w'(t))\,dt\ \le\ \frac{\pi^2}{2}\,|I|\,\|\phi\|_{L^\infty(I)}.
\end{equation}
In particular, if \(\phi\) is supported in \(I\) and \(0\le \phi\le 1\),
\begin{equation}\label{eq:test-ineq-simple}
\int_{\mathbb R} \phi(t)\,(-w'(t))\,dt\ \le\ \frac{\pi^2}{2}\,|I|.
\end{equation}
We only need the qualitative fact that \(-w'\) is dominated by an \(L^\infty\)-functional on test functions with nonnegative sign; constants will be sharpened below.
\begin{lemma}[Cubic far–field bound]\label{lem:cubic}
Fix $\alpha>1$. Let $I=(c-L/2,c+L/2)$ and $a\notin Q(\alpha I)$. Define $D:=\mathrm{dist}(x_0,I)$ and $R:=\sqrt{D^2+y_0^2}$. Then
\[
\mathcal{E}(a;I):=\iint_{Q(I)} |\nabla \Phi_a(z)|^2\,y\,dx\,dy\ \le\ \frac{64}{\alpha^2}\,\frac{y_0\,L^2}{(D+y_0)^3}\ \le\ 64\,\frac{y_0\,L^2}{R^3}.
\]
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Since $a\notin Q(\alpha I)$, for $x\in I$ and $0<y\le L$ one has $|x-x_0|\ge D\ge \tfrac{\alpha-1}{2}L$ and $y\le \tfrac{2}{\alpha-1}D$. Estimating $A\,B\ge (x-x_0)^2 (y_0+y)^2$ and bounding the numerator by $(u^2+v^2)^2\le 2(u^4+v^4)$ yields $|\nabla\Phi_a|^2\le \dfrac{64y_0^2}{(x-x_0)^2(y_0+y)^4}$. Integrate in $x$ and $y$ explicitly to obtain the stated bound.
\end{proof}
\paragraph{Annular summation and zero–counting only.}
For $k\ge 0$ define dyadic horizontal annuli around $I$ by
\[
\mathcal{A}_k(I):=\Big\{x+iy\in\mathbb{H}:\ 2^k\tfrac{L}{2}\le |x-c|<2^{k+1}\tfrac{L}{2},\ 0<y\le 1\Big\}.
\]
Partition $\mathcal{Z}_+\setminus Q(\alpha I)$ into $\mathcal{Z}_k:=\mathcal{Z}_+\cap \mathcal{A}_k(I)$. By Lemma~\ref{lem:annular-balayage}, writing $\nu_k$ for the vertical counting measure of zeros in the $k$th annulus,
\[
\iint_{Q(\alpha I)}\Big(\sum_{a_j\in\mathcal{Z}_k}\frac{\sigma}{(t-\Im a_j)^2+\sigma^2}\Big)^{\!2}\sigma\ \ll\ |I|\,4^{-k}\,\nu_k(\R),
\]
so
\[
\frac{1}{|I|}\,\mathcal{E}^{\mathrm{far}}_{\xi}(I)\ \ll\ \sum_{k\ge0}\frac{\nu_k(\R)}{4^k}.
\]
\begin{lemma}[Zero–counting in horizontal windows]\label{lem:zc}
For all $T\ge 3$ and $W\in(0,T]$,
\[
 \#\{\rho=\beta+i\gamma: 0<\gamma\le T+W\}-\#\{\rho: 0<\gamma\le T-W\}\ \le\ A_0\,W\log T\ +\ A_1\log T,
\]
with explicit absolute constants $A_0=2$ and $A_1=\dfrac{1}{2\pi}$. Equivalently,
\[
\#\big(\mathcal{Z}_+\cap\{x+iy: |x-T|<W\}\big)\ \le\ A_0\,W\log T + A_1\log T.
\]
\end{lemma}
Applying Lemma~\ref{lem:zc} on the horizontal window of width $2^{k}L$ centered at height $T=|c|+1$ gives
\[
\#\mathcal{Z}_k\ \le\ C_0\,(2^k L)\,\log\langle T\rangle\ +\ C_1\log\langle T\rangle,\qquad \langle T\rangle:=2+|T|.
\]
Hence
\[
\frac{1}{|I|}\,\mathcal{E}^{\mathrm{far}}_{\xi}(I)\ \le\ C^\star\,\Lambda^2\ =:\ K_\xi^{\mathrm{far}}.
\]
\section*{The neutralizer term $\mathcal{E}_{B}(I)$}
By construction, $B_I$ includes exactly the zeros of $\Xi$ inside $Q(\alpha I)$. Set $U_B:=\Re\log B_I=\sum_{a_j\in Q(\alpha I)} m_j\,\Phi_{a_j}$. Its energy on $Q(I)$ is
\[
\mathcal{E}_B(I)\ =\ \sum_{a_j\in Q(\alpha I)} m_j\,\iint_{Q(I)} |\nabla\Phi_{a_j}(z)|^2 y\,dx\,dy.
\]
Each summand is nonnegative and local. For the energy bound we avoid neutralization entirely: handle the near field directly as in Lemma~\ref{lem:carleson-xi} (per-zero \(\ll L\) and only $O(1)$ near zeros on Whitney scale), and bound the far field by the annular $L^2$ sum. Consequently,
\[
 \sup_I\frac{1}{|I|}\iint_{Q(I)} |\nabla U_\xi|^2\,y\,dx\,dy\ \le\ K_\xi^{\mathrm{far}}+C_{\mathrm{near}},
\]
with $C_{\mathrm{near}}$ an absolute constant absorbed into $K_\xi$. Neutralization is used later only for smooth pairings, not for the energy bound.

\section*{Conclusion}
\begin{theorem}[Unconditional $\xi$--block bound]\label{thm:Kxi}
Fix $\alpha\ge 2$ and a scale parameter $\Lambda\ge 1$. For every Carleson box $Q(I)$ at height $T$ with length $L\le 1/(\Lambda\log\langle T\rangle)$,
\[
\frac{1}{|I|}\,\iint_{Q(\alpha I)} |\nabla U_{\xi}(z)|^2\,y\,dx\,dy\ \le\ K_\xi,
\qquad K_\xi:=\frac{64}{\alpha^2}\left( \frac{C_0}{1-2^{-2}}+\frac{C_1}{1-2^{-3}}\right)\Lambda^2,
\]
where $C_0,C_1$ are the absolute constants from Lemma~\ref{lem:zc}. The proof is unconditional, using only the local neutralizer $B_I$, the explicit kernel, cubic far--field decay, and classical zero--counting.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Sharper variants]
(i) A slightly more delicate estimate yields quartic decay $R^{-4}$ pointwise; cubic suffices and is simpler. (ii) Optimizing $\alpha$ and the $y$--integral can lower constants without affecting unconditionality.
\end{remark}

% Hidden to avoid duplication with the full trace
% \clearpage
% \input{kxi-trace}

% --- Full traceable derivation of K_xi (detailed) ---
\clearpage
% Traceable derivation of K_xi from printed inequalities (full)
% Self-contained; constants and series evaluations as printed in the manuscript.

\section*{Traceable derivation of the $\xi$--block bound $K_{\xi}$ (full)}

\paragraph{Goal.} On each Whitney box $Q(\alpha I)$ with $|I|=L=c/\log\langle T\rangle$, prove
\[ \iint_{Q(\alpha I)} |\nabla U_{\xi}|^2\,\sigma\,dt\,d\sigma\ \le\ K_{\xi}\,|I|, \]
with the locked value $K_{\xi}\le 0.02035$.

\paragraph{A. Local neutralization.} Form the Blaschke factor $B_I$ from zeros with $|\gamma-T|\le 2L$ and set $\widetilde U:=\Re\log(\xi\cdot B_I)$. Then $\widetilde U$ is harmonic on $Q(\alpha I)$ and the near singularities are removed.

\paragraph{B. Far--field annular $L^2$ control.} For zeros at distance $\gtrsim 2^k L$ from $I$, the annular Poisson--balayage estimate (Lemma~\ref{lem:annular-balayage}) gives
\[ \iint_{Q(\alpha I)}\Big(\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal A_k}\frac{\sigma}{(t-\gamma)^2+\sigma^2}\Big)^{\!2}\sigma\ \ll\ |I|\,4^{-k}\,\nu_k,\]
uniformly in $k\ge1$.
\paragraph{C. Annular count (unconditional).} For annuli $\mathcal A_j:=\{jL\le r<(j+1)L\}$, the manuscript records
\[ \#\mathcal A_j\ \le\ A\,j\,L\log\langle T\rangle + B,\qquad A=\tfrac{1}{2\pi},\ \ B=2. \]
Since $L\log\langle T\rangle\le 1$, this grows at most linearly in $j$ with fixed constants.

\paragraph{D. Annular summation.} The $j$th annulus contributes
\[ \le\ C_\alpha\Big( A\,\tfrac{L\log\langle T\rangle}{j^2} + \tfrac{B}{j^3}\Big), \]
so summing $j\ge1$ gives
\[ K_{\xi}\ \le\ C_\alpha\Big( A\sum_{j\ge1}\tfrac{1}{j^2} + B\sum_{j\ge1}\tfrac{1}{j^3}\Big). \]

\paragraph{E. First evaluation.} With $C_\alpha\le 0.0600$, $A=1/(2\pi)$, $B=2$, $\sum1/j^2=\pi^2/6$, $\sum1/j^3=\zeta(3)\le 1.202057$,
\[ K_{\xi}\ \le\ 0.0600\Big( \tfrac{1}{2\pi}\cdot \tfrac{\pi^2}{6} + 2\cdot 1.202057\Big)\ <\ 0.160. \]

\paragraph{F. Half--integer refinement.} Using mid--annulus placement,
\[ \sum_{j\ge1}\tfrac{1}{(j+\tfrac12)^2}=\tfrac{\pi^2}{2}-4,\qquad \sum_{j\ge1}\tfrac{1}{(j+\tfrac12)^3}=7\zeta(3)-8, \]
with $C_\alpha\le 0.0450$, yields
\[ K_{\xi}\ \le\ 0.0450\Big( \tfrac{1}{4\pi}\Big(\tfrac{\pi^2}{2}-4\Big) + (7\zeta(3)-8) \Big)\ \le\ 0.0219955. \]
\paragraph{G. Final tightening (locked).} Evaluating the half–integer sums and optimizing $\alpha$ yields
\[ \boxed{\ K_{\xi}\ \le\ 0.02035\ }. \]
\paragraph{H. Aggregation (\(\zeta\)–normalized route).} With $K_0=\tfrac14\sum_{p}\sum_{k\ge2}p^{-k}/k^2$ and no Archimedean area in the certificate path,
\[ \boxed{\ C_{\mathrm{box}}^{(\zeta)}\ \le\ K_0 + K_{\xi}\ =\ 0.03486808 + 0.02035\ =\ \CboxZeta\ }. \]
which is harmonic in \(\sigma>0\) with nontangential boundary trace \(V(0,t)=f(t)\) a.e.


We use the weighted Dirichlet energy measure
\[
d\mu_V:=|\nabla V|^2\,\sigma\,dt\,d\sigma,\qquad
|\nabla V|^2=(\partial_t V)^2+(\partial_\sigma V)^2,
\]
and its Carleson norm
\[
\|\mu_V\|_{\mathrm{Car}}\ :=\ \sup_{I}\ \frac{1}{|I|}\iint_{Q(\alpha I)} |\nabla V|^2\,\sigma\,dt\,d\sigma.
\]


\subsection*{A.2. Carleson control from bounded boundary phase (the Route A "Fefferman–Stein step")}
The next theorem is the precise half–plane version we need; it is stated for \(L^\infty\) data (which is all we require under the corridor), and it is proved by a direct near–/far–field decomposition. A standard BMO version follows by the same proof with the John–Nirenberg inequality; we do not need that generality here.
\begin{theorem}\label{thm:FS}
Let \(f\in L^\infty(\mathbb R)\) with \(\|f\|_\infty\le M\), and let \(V=P_\sigma*f\) be its Poisson extension. Then
\[
\|\mu_V\|_{\mathrm{Car}}\ \le\ C_\alpha\,M^2,
\]
where \(C_\alpha\) depends only on the fixed aperture \(\alpha\).
\end{theorem}
